England</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">Population<div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;"><span style="white-space: nowrap"><a class="external text" href="/wiki/List_of_MPs_elected_in_the_2017_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="List of MPs elected in the 2017 United Kingdom general election">MPs</a></th><td><div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none; padding: 0;">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">List of MPs</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align:left;display:none; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Philip_Davies" title="Philip Davies">Philip Davies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Con</a>)</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Naz_Shah" title="Naz Shah">Naz Shah</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Lab</a>)</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/John_Grogan_(politician)" title="John Grogan (politician)">John Grogan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Lab</a>)</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Judith_Cummins" title="Judith Cummins">Judith Cummins</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Lab</a>)</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Imran_Hussain_(British_politician)" title="Imran Hussain (British politician)">Imran Hussain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Lab</a>)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Yorkshire and the Humber (European Parliament constituency)">Yorkshire and the Humber</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bradford.gov.uk/">www.bradford.gov.uk</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Bradford</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-Bradford.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/En-uk-Bradford.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-Bradford.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> is a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>, England, in the foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>, 8.6 miles (14&#160;km) west of <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, and 16 miles (26&#160;km) north-west of <a href="/wiki/Wakefield" title="Wakefield">Wakefield</a>. Bradford became a municipal borough in 1847, and received its charter as a city in 1897. Following <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">local government reform</a> in 1974, <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a> was bestowed upon the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford" title="City of Bradford">City of Bradford</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_borough" title="Metropolitan borough">metropolitan borough</a>.
</p><p>Bradford forms part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Urban_Area" title="West Yorkshire Urban Area">West Yorkshire Urban Area</a>, which in 2001 had a population of 1.5&#160;million and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of urban areas in the United Kingdom">fourth largest in the United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Bradford itself has a population of 529,870, which makes it the seventh-largest city in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the third-largest city in <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> after <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">Historically</a> part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding of Yorkshire</a>, Bradford rose to prominence in the 19th century as an international centre of <a href="/wiki/Textile_manufacture_during_the_Industrial_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Textile manufacture during the Industrial Revolution">textile manufacture</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>. It was a <a href="/wiki/Boomtown" title="Boomtown">boomtown</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and amongst the earliest <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialised</a> settlements, rapidly becoming the "wool capital of the world".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The area's access to a supply of coal, iron ore and soft water facilitated the growth of Bradford's manufacturing base, which, as textile manufacture grew, led to an explosion in population and was a stimulus to civic investment; Bradford has a large amount of listed <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian architecture</a> including the grand Italianate <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Hall" title="Bradford City Hall">City Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The textile sector in Bradford fell into decline from the mid-20th century. Bradford has since emerged as a tourist destination, becoming the first <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/City_of_Film" title="City of Film">City of Film</a> with attractions such as the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Park" title="Bradford City Park">Bradford City Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Alhambra" title="Bradford Alhambra">Alhambra theatre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cartwright_Hall" title="Cartwright Hall">Cartwright Hall</a>. Bradford has faced similar challenges to the rest of <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">post-industrial</a> <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Deindustrialisation">deindustrialisation</a>, social unrest and economic deprivation.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Bradford" title="Timeline of Bradford">Timeline of Bradford</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span></h3>
<p>The name Bradford is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> <i>brad</i> and <i>ford</i> the broad <a href="/wiki/Ford_(crossing)" title="Ford (crossing)">ford</a> which referred to a crossing of the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Beck" title="Bradford Beck">Bradford Beck</a> at Church Bank below the site of <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">Bradford Cathedral</a>, around which a settlement grew in Saxon times.<sup id="cite_ref-visitbradford.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitbradford.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It was recorded as "Bradeford" in 1086.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<p>After an <a href="/wiki/Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Uprising">uprising</a> in 1070, during <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Harrying_of_the_North" title="Harrying of the North">Harrying of the North</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Manorialism" title="Manorialism">manor</a> of Bradford was laid <a href="/wiki/Manor#Constituent_lands" title="Manor">waste</a><sup id="cite_ref-visitbradford.com_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitbradford.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and is described as such in the <i><a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a></i> of 1086. It then became part of the <i>Honour of Pontefract</i> given to <a href="/wiki/Ilbert_de_Lacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilbert de Lacy">Ilbert de Lacy</a> for service to the Conqueror, in whose family the manor remained until 1311.<sup id="cite_ref-visitbradford.com_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitbradford.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> There is evidence of a castle in the time of the Lacys.<sup id="cite_ref-tde_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tde-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The manor then passed to the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Lincoln" title="Earl of Lincoln">Earl of Lincoln</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_of_Gaunt" title="John of Gaunt">John of Gaunt</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">The Crown</a> and, ultimately, private ownership in 1620.<sup id="cite_ref-visitbradford.com_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitbradford.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the <a href="/wiki/Middle_ages" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle ages">middle ages</a> Bradford, had become a small town centred on Kirkgate, Westgate and Ivegate.<sup id="cite_ref-visitbradford.com_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitbradford.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheeran200513_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheeran200513-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 1316 there is mention of a <a href="/wiki/Fulling" title="Fulling">fulling</a> mill, a soke mill where all the manor corn was milled and a market. During the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a> the inhabitants sided with <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lancaster" title="House of Lancaster">House of Lancaster</a>. <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">Edward IV</a> granted the right to hold two annual fairs and from this time the town began to prosper. In the reign of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a> Bradford exceeded Leeds as a manufacturing centre.<sup id="cite_ref-tde_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tde-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Bradford grew slowly over the next two-hundred years as the <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">woollen</a> trade gained in prominence.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">Civil War</a> the town was garrisoned for the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a> and in 1642 was unsuccessfully attacked by <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Royalist</a> forces from Leeds. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fairfax,_3rd_Lord_Fairfax_of_Cameron" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Fairfax, 3rd Lord Fairfax of Cameron">Sir Thomas Fairfax</a> took the command of the garrison and marched to meet the <a href="/wiki/William_Cavendish,_1st_Duke_of_Newcastle-upon-Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="William Cavendish, 1st Duke of Newcastle-upon-Tyne">Duke of Newcastle</a> but was defeated. The Parliamentarians retreated to Bradford and the Royalists set up headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Bolling_Hall,_Bradford" title="Bolling Hall, Bradford">Bolling Hall</a> from where the town was besieged leading to its surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-tde_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tde-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Civil War caused a decline in industry but after the accession of <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William III</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_II_of_England" title="Mary II of England">Mary II</a> in 1689 prosperity began to return.<sup id="cite_ref-visitbradford.com_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitbradford.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The launch of manufacturing in the early 18th century marked the start of the town's development while new <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turnpike_road" class="mw-redirect" title="Turnpike road">turnpike road</a> links encouraged trade.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_Revolution">Industrial Revolution</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Map of Bradford boundaries in 1835." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg/220px-Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg/330px-Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg/440px-Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Creighton_bradford_1835.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bradford Boundaries 1835.</div></div></div><p> In 1801, Bradford was a rural <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market town</a> of 6,393 people,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheeran200511_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheeran200511-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> where wool spinning and cloth weaving was carried out in local cottages and farms. Bradford was thus not much bigger than nearby <a href="/wiki/Keighley" title="Keighley">Keighley</a> (5,745) and was significantly smaller than <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a> (8,866) and <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a> (7,268).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheeran200511_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheeran200511-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This small town acted as a hub for three nearby townships – <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bowling_and_Barkerend" title="Bowling and Barkerend">Bowling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Horton" title="Great Horton">Great</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Horton" title="Little Horton">Little Horton</a>, which were separated from the town by countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheeran200511_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheeran200511-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Blast_furnace" title="Blast furnace">Blast furnaces</a> were established in about 1788 by Hird, Dawson Hardy at <a href="/wiki/Low_Moor,_Bradford" title="Low Moor, Bradford">Low Moor</a> and iron was worked by the <a href="/wiki/Bowling_Iron_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Bowling Iron Company">Bowling Iron Company</a> until about 1900. Yorkshire iron was used for shackles, hooks and piston rods for locomotives, colliery cages and other mining appliances where toughness was required. The <a href="/wiki/Low_Moor_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Low Moor Company">Low Moor Company</a> also made <a href="/wiki/Pig_iron" title="Pig iron">pig iron</a> and the company employed 1,500 men in 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-GG_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GG-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> when the municipal borough of Bradford was created in 1847 there were 46 coal mines within its boundaries. Coal output continued to expand, reaching a peak in 1868 when Bradford contributed a quarter of all the coal and iron produced in Yorkshire.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The population of the township in 1841 was 34,560.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1825 the wool-combers union called a strike that lasted five-months but workers were forced to return to work through hardship leading to the introduction of machine-combing.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> led to rapid growth, with wool imported in vast quantities for the manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Worsted" title="Worsted">worsted</a> cloth in which Bradford specialised, and the town soon became known as the wool capital of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-brad.ac.uk_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brad.ac.uk-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A permanent military presence was established in the city with the completion of <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Moor_Barracks" title="Bradford Moor Barracks">Bradford Moor Barracks</a> in 1844.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg/220px-Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="348" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg/330px-Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg/440px-Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6460" data-file-height="10232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_waterworks_map_1881.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bradford waterworks on completion of the Wharfedale scheme in 1881</div></div></div>
<p>Bradford had  ample supplies of locally mined coal to provide the power that the industry needed. Local <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> was an excellent resource for building the mills, and with a population of 182,000 by 1850,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> the town grew rapidly as workers were attracted by jobs in the textile mills.<sup id="cite_ref-brad.ac.uk_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brad.ac.uk-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> A desperate shortage of water in <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Dale_(Yorkshire)" title="Bradford Dale (Yorkshire)">Bradford Dale</a>  was a serious limitation on industrial expansion and improvement in urban sanitary conditions. In 1854 Bradford  Corporation bought the Bradford Water Company<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and embarked on a huge engineering programme to bring supplies of soft water from Airedale, Wharfedale and <a href="/wiki/Nidd_Aqueduct" title="Nidd Aqueduct">Nidderdale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> By 1882 water supply had radically improved. Meanwhile, urban expansion took place along the routes out of the city towards the Hortons and Bowling and the townships had become part of a continuous urban area by the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheeran200513_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheeran200513-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A major employer was <a href="/wiki/Titus_Salt" title="Titus Salt">Titus Salt</a> who in 1833 took over the running of his father's woollen business specialising in fabrics combining <a href="/wiki/Alpaca" title="Alpaca">alpaca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohair" title="Mohair">mohair</a>, cotton and silk. By 1850 he had five mills. However, because of the polluted environment and squalid conditions for his workers Salt left Bradford and transferred his business to <a href="/wiki/Salts_Mill" title="Salts Mill">Salts Mill</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saltaire" title="Saltaire">Saltaire</a> in 1850, where in 1853 he began to build the workers' village which has become a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage site">UNESCO World Heritage site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Ripley" title="Henry Ripley">Henry Ripley</a> was a younger contemporary of Titus Salt. He was managing partner of Edward Ripley &amp; Son Ltd, which owned the Bowling Dye Works. In 1880 the dye works employed over 1000 people and was said to be the biggest dye works in Europe. Like Salt he was a councillor, JP and Bradford MP who was deeply concerned to improve working class housing conditions. He built the industrial <a href="/wiki/Model_village" title="Model village">Model village</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ripley_Ville" title="Ripley Ville">Ripley Ville</a> on a site in <a href="/wiki/Broomfields,_Bradford" title="Broomfields, Bradford">Broomfields</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Bowling" title="East Bowling">East Bowling</a> close to the dye works.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Listermillsbradford.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Listermillsbradford.jpg/220px-Listermillsbradford.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Listermillsbradford.jpg/330px-Listermillsbradford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Listermillsbradford.jpg/440px-Listermillsbradford.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Listermillsbradford.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lister%27s_Mill" class="mw-redirect" title="Lister&#39;s Mill">Lister's Mill</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce,_Little_Germany.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce%2C_Little_Germany.jpg/150px-Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce%2C_Little_Germany.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce%2C_Little_Germany.jpg/225px-Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce%2C_Little_Germany.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce%2C_Little_Germany.jpg/300px-Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce%2C_Little_Germany.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Chamber_of_Commerce,_Little_Germany.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Little_Germany,_Bradford" title="Little Germany, Bradford">Little Germany</a></div></div></div>
<p>Other major employers were <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Lister,_1st_Baron_Masham" title="Samuel Lister, 1st Baron Masham">Samuel Lister</a> and his brother who were worsted <a href="/wiki/Spinning_(textiles)" title="Spinning (textiles)">spinners</a> and manufacturers at <a href="/wiki/Lister_Mills" title="Lister Mills">Lister's Mill</a> (Manningham Mills). Lister epitomised <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> enterprise but it has been suggested that his <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> attitude made <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a> necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
Unprecedented growth created problems with over 200 factory chimneys continually churning out black, sulphurous smoke, Bradford gained the reputation of being the most polluted town in England. There were frequent outbreaks of cholera and typhoid, and only 30% of children born to textile workers reached the age of fifteen. This extreme level of <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant</a> and youth mortality contributed to a life expectancy for Bradford residents of just over eighteen years, which was one of the lowest in the country.
</p><p>Like many major cities Bradford has been a destination for immigrants. In the 1840s Bradford's population was significantly increased by migrants from Ireland, particularly rural <a href="/wiki/County_Mayo" title="County Mayo">Mayo</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sligo" title="Sligo">Sligo</a>, and by 1851 about 10% of the population were born in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, the largest proportion in <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
Around <sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  the middle decades of the 19th century the Irish were concentrated in eight densely settled areas situated near the town centre. One of these was the Bedford Street area of <a href="/wiki/Broomfields" title="Broomfields">Broomfields</a> which in 1861 contained 1,162 persons of Irish birth—19% of all Irish born persons in the Borough.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 1820s and 1830s, there was immigration from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. Many were <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Merchants" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchants">merchants</a> and they became active in the life of the town. The Jewish community mostly living in the <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham</a> area of the town,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> numbered about 100 families but was influential in the development of Bradford as a major exporter of woollen goods from their textile export houses predominately based in <a href="/wiki/Little_Germany,_Bradford" title="Little Germany, Bradford">Little Germany</a> and the civic life of Bradford. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Semon" title="Charles Semon">Charles Semon</a> (1814–1877) was a textile merchant and philanthropist who developed a productive textile export house in the town, he became the first foreign and Jewish mayor of Bradford in 1864.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Behrens" title="Jacob Behrens">Jacob Behrens</a> (1806–1889) was the first foreign textile merchant to export woollen goods from the town, his company developed into an international multimillion-pound business.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Behrens was a philanthropist, he also helped to establish the Bradford chamber of commerce in 1851.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Moser" title="Jacob Moser">Jacob Moser</a> (1839 – 1922) was a textile merchant who was a partner in the firm Edelstein, Moser and Co, which developed into a successful Bradford textile export house. Moser was a  philanthropist, he founded the Bradford Charity Organisation Society and the City Guild of Help. In 1910 Moser became the first Jewish Lord Mayor of Bradford.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg/150px-Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg/225px-Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg/300px-Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jowett_Eight_badge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jowett" class="mw-redirect" title="Jowett">Jowett</a> Cars Eight badge</div></div></div>
<p>To support the textile <a href="/wiki/Mill_(factory)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mill (factory)">mills</a>, a large manufacturing base grew up in the town providing textile machinery, and this led to diversification with different industries thriving side by side.<sup id="cite_ref-brad.ac.uk_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brad.ac.uk-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jowett" class="mw-redirect" title="Jowett">Jowett</a> Motor Company founded in the early 20th century by Benjamin and William Jowett and Arthur V Lamb, manufactured cars and vans in Bradford for 50 years.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Scott_Motorcycle_Company" title="The Scott Motorcycle Company">The Scott Motorcycle Company</a> was a well known producer of motorcycles and light engines for industry. Founded by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Angas_Scott" title="Alfred Angas Scott">Alfred Angas Scott</a> in 1908 as the Scott Engineering Company in Bradford, Scott motorcycles were produced until 1978.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_Labour_Party">Independent Labour Party</span></h3>
<p>The city played an important part in the early history of the Labour Party. A mural on the back of the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Playhouse" title="Bradford Playhouse">Bradford Playhouse</a> in <a href="/wiki/Little_Germany,_Bradford" title="Little Germany, Bradford">Little Germany</a> commemorates the centenary of the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Labour_Party" title="Independent Labour Party">Independent Labour Party</a> in Bradford in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bradford_Pals">The Bradford Pals</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:14th_Foot_colours.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/14th_Foot_colours.jpg/220px-14th_Foot_colours.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/14th_Foot_colours.jpg/330px-14th_Foot_colours.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/14th_Foot_colours.jpg/440px-14th_Foot_colours.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1592" data-file-height="1329" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:14th_Foot_colours.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regimental colours</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Pals_battalions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Pals battalions">The Bradford Pals</a> were three First World War <a href="/wiki/Pals_battalion" title="Pals battalion">Pals battalions</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kitchener%27s_Army" title="Kitchener&#39;s Army">Kitchener's Army</a> raised in the city. When the three battalions were taken over by the British Army they were officially named the 16th (1st Bradford), 18th (2nd Bradford), and 20th (Reserve) Battalions, <a href="/wiki/The_Prince_of_Wales%27s_Own_(West_Yorkshire_Regiment)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Prince of Wales&#39;s Own (West Yorkshire Regiment)">The Prince of Wales's Own (West Yorkshire Regiment)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the morning of 1 July 1916, the 16th and 18th Battalions left their trenches in Northern France to advance across No Man's Land. It was the first hour of the <a href="/wiki/First_day_on_the_Somme" title="First day on the Somme">First day of the Battle of the Somme</a>. Of the estimated 1,394 men from Bradford and District in the two battalions, 1,060 were either killed or injured during the ill-fated attack on the village of <a href="/wiki/Serre-l%C3%A8s-Puisieux" title="Serre-lès-Puisieux">Serre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other Bradford Battalions of The Prince of Wales's Own (West Yorkshire Regiment) involved in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a> were the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Rifles" title="Bradford Rifles">1st/6th Battalion</a> (the former <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Rifles" title="Bradford Rifles">Bradford Rifle Volunteers</a>), part of the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Force" title="Territorial Force">Territorial Force</a>, based at <a href="/wiki/Belle_Vue,_Bradford" title="Belle Vue, Bradford">Belle Vue Barracks</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham</a>, and the 10th Battalion (another Kitchener battalion).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orbat_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orbat-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The 1/6th Battalion first saw action in 1915 at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aubers_Ridge" title="Battle of Aubers Ridge">Battle of Aubers Ridge</a> before moving north to the <a href="/wiki/Ieperlee" title="Ieperlee">Yser Canal</a> near <a href="/wiki/Ypres" title="Ypres">Ypres</a>. On the first day of the Somme they took heavy casualties while trying to support the <a href="/wiki/36th_(Ulster)_Division" title="36th (Ulster) Division">36th (Ulster) Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The 10th Battalion was involved in the attack on <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Fricourt" title="Capture of Fricourt">Fricourt</a>, where it suffered the highest casualty rate of any battalion on the Somme on 1 July and perhaps the highest battalion casualty list for a single day during the entire war. Nearly 60% of the battalion's casualties were deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1/2nd and 2/2nd <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_Artillery" title="West Riding Artillery">West Riding Brigades</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Field_Artillery" title="Royal Field Artillery">Royal Field Artillery</a> (TF), had their headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a> in Manningham, with batteries at Bradford, <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heckmondwike" title="Heckmondwike">Heckmondwike</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The 1/2nd Brigade crossed to France with the 1/6th Battalion West Yorks in April 1915. These Territorial Force units were to remain close to each other throughout the war, serving in the <a href="/wiki/49th_(West_Riding)_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="49th (West Riding) Division">49th (West Riding) Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> They were joined in 1917 by the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Rifles" title="Bradford Rifles">2/6th Battalion, West Yorks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_Artillery" title="West Riding Artillery">2/2nd West Riding Brigade, RFA</a>, serving in the <a href="/wiki/62nd_(2nd_West_Riding)_Division" title="62nd (2nd West Riding) Division">62nd (2nd West Riding) Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morrisons_HQ,_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Morrisons_HQ%2C_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg/220px-Morrisons_HQ%2C_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Morrisons_HQ%2C_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg/330px-Morrisons_HQ%2C_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Morrisons_HQ%2C_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg/440px-Morrisons_HQ%2C_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="463" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morrisons_HQ,_Bradford_-_geograph.org.uk_-_372718.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Morrisons' headquarters in Bradford</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> migrants came from <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and since the 1950s from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and particularly <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bradlibs.com_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bradlibs.com-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The textile industry has been in decline throughout the latter part of the 20th century. A culture of innovation had been fundamental to Bradford's dominance, with new textile technologies being invented in the city; a prime example being the work of <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Lister,_1st_Baron_Masham" title="Samuel Lister, 1st Baron Masham">Samuel Lister</a>. This innovation culture continues today throughout Bradford's economy, from automotive (Kahn Design)<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> to electronics (<a href="/wiki/Pace_Micro_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Pace Micro Technology">Pace Micro Technology</a>).
<a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Wm Morrison Supermarkets</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/William_Morrison_(businessman)" title="William Morrison (businessman)">William Morrison</a> in 1899, initially as an egg and butter merchant in Rawson Market, operating under the name of <i>Wm Morrison (Provisions) Limited</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-student_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-student-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The grandest of the mills no longer used for textile production is Lister's Mill, the chimney of which can be seen from most places in Bradford. It has become a beacon of regeneration after a £100&#160;million conversion to apartment blocks by property developer <a href="/wiki/Urban_Splash" title="Urban Splash">Urban Splash</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1989, copies of <a href="/wiki/Salman_Rushdie" title="Salman Rushdie">Salman Rushdie</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Satanic_Verses" title="The Satanic Verses">The Satanic Verses</a></i> were burnt in the city, and a section of the <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> community led a campaign against the book. In July 2001, ethnic tensions led to <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Riots" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford Riots">rioting</a>, and a report described Bradford as fragmented<sup id="cite_ref-fairuk.org_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fairuk.org-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and a city of segregated ethnic communities.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Building_Society" title="Yorkshire Building Society">Yorkshire Building Society</a> opened its new headquarters in the city in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006 Wm <a href="/wiki/Morrison_Supermarkets" class="mw-redirect" title="Morrison Supermarkets">Morrison Supermarkets</a> opened its new headquarters in the city, the firm employs more than 5,000 people in Bradford.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2009 Bradford became the world's first <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/City_of_Film" title="City of Film">City of Film</a> and became part of the <a href="/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network" title="Creative Cities Network">Creative Cities Network</a> since then.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The city has a long history of producing both films and the technology that produces moving film which includes the invention of the Cieroscope, which took place in Manningham in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010 <a href="/wiki/Provident_Financial" title="Provident Financial">Provident Financial</a> opened its new headquarters in the city. The company has been based in the city since 1880.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012 the <a href="/wiki/British_Wool_Marketing_Board" title="British Wool Marketing Board">British Wool Marketing Board</a> opened its new headquarters in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2012 <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Park" title="Bradford City Park">Bradford City Park</a> opened, the park which cost £24.5 million to construct is a public space in the city centre which features numerous fountains and a mirror pool surrounded by benches and a walk way.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015 <a href="/wiki/The_Broadway,_Bradford" title="The Broadway, Bradford">The Broadway</a> opened, the shopping and leisure complex in the centre of Bradford cost £260 million to build and is owned by <a href="/wiki/Meyer_Bergman" title="Meyer Bergman">Meyer Bergman</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2016</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford" title="City of Bradford">City of Bradford</a></div>
<p>Bradford is represented by three MPs: for the constituencies of <a href="/wiki/Bradford_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bradford East (UK Parliament constituency)">Bradford East</a> (<a href="/wiki/Imran_Hussain_(British_politician)" title="Imran Hussain (British politician)">Imran Hussain</a>, Labour Party), <a href="/wiki/Bradford_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bradford South (UK Parliament constituency)">Bradford South</a> (<a href="/wiki/Judith_Cummins" title="Judith Cummins">Judith Cummins</a>, Labour), and <a href="/wiki/Bradford_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bradford West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bradford West</a> (<a href="/wiki/Naz_Shah" title="Naz Shah">Naz Shah</a>, Labour Party).
</p><p>Bradford is within the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Yorkshire and the Humber (European Parliament constituency)">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> European constituency, which is represented by two <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> MEPs, two <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">Ukip</a> MEPs.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The election results for Bradford in the <a href="/wiki/2009_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="2009 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">European Parliament election</a> in June 2009 were: Conservative 19.2%, Labour 29.3%, UKIP 31.1%, Lib Dem 6.25%, <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green</a> 7.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2014 election, the figures were Conservative 16.5% (-8.2% from 2009 election), Labour 39.4% (+16.9%), Liberal Democrat 7.0% (-6.4%), UKIP 24.8% (9.9%), Green 6.8% (-2.0%), BNP 1.4% (-7.9%), SNP/PC 0.0% (0.0%), Others 4.0% (-2.3%); total votes cast 128,787; number of electorate 342,381; turnout 37.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_of_the_Independent_Labour_Party.svg" class="image" title="150pxl"><img alt="150pxl" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Logo_of_the_Independent_Labour_Party.svg/161px-Logo_of_the_Independent_Labour_Party.svg.png" decoding="async" width="161" height="161" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Logo_of_the_Independent_Labour_Party.svg/242px-Logo_of_the_Independent_Labour_Party.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Logo_of_the_Independent_Labour_Party.svg/322px-Logo_of_the_Independent_Labour_Party.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="161" data-file-height="161" /></a></div>
<p>The city played an important part in the early history of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>. A mural on the back of the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Playhouse" title="Bradford Playhouse">Bradford Playhouse</a> (visible from Leeds Road) commemorates the centenary of the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Labour_Party" title="Independent Labour Party">Independent Labour Party</a> in 1893, and quotes its motto "There is no weal save commonweal".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The original Bradford Coat of Arms had the Latin words <a href="/wiki/Labor_omnia_vincit" title="Labor omnia vincit">Labor omnia vincit</a> below it, meaning "Work conquers all".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> A new coat of arms was emblazoned in 1976, after local government reorganisation in 1974, with the English motto "Progress, Industry, Humanity".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<p>Bradford is located at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Bradford&amp;params=53_45_00_N_01_50_00_W_type:city(293000)_region:GB"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°45′00″N</span> <span class="longitude">01°50′00″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.75000°N 1.83333°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.75000; -1.83333</span></span></span></a></span> (53.7500, -1.8333)<a href="/wiki/World_gazetteer" class="mw-redirect" title="World gazetteer"><sup>1</sup></a>. Topographically, it is located in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> region of the <a href="/wiki/South_Pennines" title="South Pennines">South Pennines</a>.
</p><p>Bradford is not built on any substantial body of water but is situated at the junction of three valleys, one of them, that of the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Beck" title="Bradford Beck">Bradford Beck</a> which rises in <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a> to the west, and is swelled by its tributaries, the Horton Beck, Westbrook, Bowling Beck and Eastbrook. At the site of the original ford, the beck turns north, and flows towards the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">River Aire</a> at <a href="/wiki/Shipley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Shipley, West Yorkshire">Shipley</a>. Bradfordale (or Bradforddale) is a name given to this valley (see for example Firth 1997<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Firth"><a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bradford#endnote_Firth">[5]</a></sup>). It can be regarded as one of the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Dales" title="Yorkshire Dales">Yorkshire Dales</a>, though as it passes though the city, it is often not recognised as such. The beck's course through the city centre is <a href="/wiki/Culvert" title="Culvert">culverted</a> and has been since the mid 19th century. On the 1852 <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey" title="Ordnance Survey">Ordnance Survey</a> map<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_OS_1852"><a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bradford#endnote_OS_1852">[6]</a></sup> it is visible as far as Sun Bridge, at the end of Tyrrell Street, and then from beside <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Bradford Forster Square railway station</a> on Kirkgate. On the 1906 Ordnance Survey,<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_OS_1906"><a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bradford#endnote_OS_1906">[7]</a></sup> it disappears at Tumbling Hill Street, off Thornton Road, and appears north of Cape Street, off Valley Road, though there are culverts as far as Queens Road.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Canal" title="Bradford Canal">Bradford Canal</a>, built in 1774, linking the city to the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> took its water from Bradford Beck and its tributaries. The supply was often inadequate to feed the locks, and the polluted state of the canal led to its temporary closure in 1866: the canal was closed in the early 20th century as uneconomic.
</p>

</tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>
<p>The underlying geology of the city is primarily <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">carboniferous</a> <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstones</a>. These vary in quality from rough rock to fine, honey-coloured stone of building quality. Access to this material has had a pronounced effect on the architecture of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheeran20059_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheeran20059-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The city also lies within the north western parts of the <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire_Coalfield" title="South Yorkshire Coalfield">Yorkshire Coalfield</a> which is mostly composed of carboniferous <a href="/wiki/Coal_measures" title="Coal measures">coal measures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<p>As with the vast majority of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a>, Bradford experiences a <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: <i>Cfb</i>), with limited seasonal temperature ranges, and generally moderate rainfall throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Records have been collected since 1908 from the <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office's</a> weather station at Lister Park, a short distance north of the city centre. This constitutes one of the nation's longest unbroken records of daily data. The full record can be found on the council's website.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG/220px-Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG/330px-Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG/440px-Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lister_Park_weather_station.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The weather station enclosure at Lister Park</div></div></div>
<p>The absolute maximum temperature recorded was 32.2&#160;°C (90.0&#160;°F) in August 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In an 'average' year, the warmest day should attain a temperature of 27.5&#160;°C (81.5&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> with a total of 6 days<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> rising to a maximum of 25.1&#160;°C (77.2&#160;°F) or above.
</p><p>The absolute minimum temperature recorded was −13.9&#160;°C (7.0&#160;°F) during January 1940. The weather station's elevated suburban location means exceptionally low temperatures are unknown. Typically, 41.4 nights of the year will record an air frost.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Rainfall averages around 870&#160;mm (34&#160;in) per year with over 1&#160;mm falling on 139 days.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sunshine, at little in excess of 1,250 hours per year is low, as one would expect of an inland location in Northern England located amongst upland areas. All averages refer to the 1981–2010 observation period.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_belt">Green belt</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/South_and_West_Yorkshire_Green_Belt" title="South and West Yorkshire Green Belt">South and West Yorkshire Green Belt</a></div>
<p>Bradford is within a <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">green belt</a> region that extends into the borough and wider surrounding counties. It is in place to reduce <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, prevent the towns in the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Urban_Area" title="West Yorkshire Urban Area">West Yorkshire Urban Area</a> conurbation from further convergence, protect the identity of outlying communities, encourage <a href="/wiki/Brownfield" class="mw-redirect" title="Brownfield">brownfield</a> reuse, and preserve nearby countryside. This is achieved by restricting inappropriate development within the designated areas, and imposing stricter conditions on permitted building.<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The green belt surrounds the Bradford built-up area, separating towns and villages throughout the borough. Larger outlying communities such as <a href="/wiki/Bingley" title="Bingley">Bingley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilsden" title="Wilsden">Wilsden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cottingley,_Bradford" title="Cottingley, Bradford">Cottingley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thornton,_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Thornton, Bradford">Thornton</a> are also exempt from the green belt area. However, nearby smaller villages, hamlets and rural areas such as Brunthwaite, Keelham, Denholme Gate, <a href="/wiki/Laycock,_West_Yorkshire" title="Laycock, West Yorkshire">Laycock Esholt</a>, Micklethwaite, <a href="/wiki/Goose_Eye" class="mw-redirect" title="Goose Eye">Goose Eye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanbury" title="Stanbury">Stanbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hainworth" title="Hainworth">Hainworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tong,_West_Yorkshire" title="Tong, West Yorkshire">Tong</a>, and Harecroft are 'washed over' by the designation.<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Much semi-rural land on the fringes is also included. The area in 2017 amounted to some 23,890 hectares (238.9&#160;km<sup>2</sup>; 92.2&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A subsidiary aim of the green belt is to encourage recreation and leisure interests,<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> with rural landscape features, greenfield areas and facilities including Park Wood; <a href="/wiki/Northcliffe_Park" title="Northcliffe Park">Northcliffe park and woods</a>; <a href="/wiki/Heaton_Woods" title="Heaton Woods">Heaton Woods</a>; Chellow Dene woods and reservoirs; Horton Bank country park; Norr Hill; Gilstead recreation park; Stone Circle remains by Shipley Glen; <a href="/wiki/Bracken_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Bracken Hall">Bracken Hall</a>; River Aire valley; Leeds and Liverpool canal; and the Leeds Country Way.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span></h2>
<table class="box-Off_topic plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>may <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Guide_to_writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Guide to writing better articles">stray from the topic</a> of the article</b>&#160;into the topic of another article, <i><a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford" title="City of Bradford">City of Bradford</a></i>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bradford&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> or discuss this issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Bradford" title="Talk:Bradford">talk page</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2011</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Bradford" title="Demography of Bradford">Demography of Bradford</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png/220px-Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png/330px-Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png/440px-Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png 2x" data-file-width="18266" data-file-height="17494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population density in the Bradford Metropolitan District Council Area from the 2011 census</div></div></div>
<p>At the 2011 UK census, Bradford had a population of 522,452.<sup id="cite_ref-bradford.gov.uk_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bradford.gov.uk-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> There were 106,680 <a href="/wiki/Households" class="mw-redirect" title="Households">households</a> in Bradford, and the <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 4,560 inhabitants per square kilometre (11,820/sq mi). For every 100 females, there were 92.9 males.<sup id="cite_ref-statistics.gov.uk_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics.gov.uk-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Bradford has the youngest, fastest growing population outside London.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The census showed that of Bradford's total population, 67.44% (352,317) was <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White</a>, 26.83% (140,149) <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a>, 2.48% (12,979) <a href="/wiki/Mixed_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed Race">Mixed Race</a>, 1.77% (9,267) <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black</a> and 1.48% (7,740) from other races.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>22.1% of the population are <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">British Asian</a> (included in the 26.83% "Asian" figure above), the third-highest percentage of <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asians</a> in a single settlement in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a> (behind the city of <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a> at 29.9% and the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Tower_Hamlets" title="London Borough of Tower Hamlets">London Borough of Tower Hamlets</a>).
Nearly half of all Asians living in <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> live in Bradford, with the central wards of <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Moor" title="Bradford Moor">Bradford Moor</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_(ward)" title="City (ward)">City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Little_Horton" title="Little Horton">Little Horton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toller" title="Toller">Toller</a> having large majority Asian populations, whereas outlying wards of Bradford such as <a href="/wiki/Thornton,_West_Yorkshire" title="Thornton, West Yorkshire">Thornton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allerton,_West_Yorkshire" title="Allerton, West Yorkshire">Allerton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idle,_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Idle, Bradford">Idle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thackley" title="Thackley">Thackley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eccleshill,_West_Yorkshire" title="Eccleshill, West Yorkshire">Eccleshill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wibsey" title="Wibsey">Wibsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyke" title="Wyke">Wyke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clayton,_West_Yorkshire" title="Clayton, West Yorkshire">Clayton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrose" title="Wrose">Wrose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tong_(ward)" title="Tong (ward)">Tong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royds,_Bradford" title="Royds, Bradford">Royds</a> have predominantly <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> <a href="/wiki/Populations" class="mw-redirect" title="Populations">populations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
