<td style="text-align:right;">0.8
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Total
</td>
<td style="text-align:right;">522,452
</td>
<td style="text-align:right;">100
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Office for National Statistics Regional Trends report, published in June 2009, showed that some parts of Bradford suffer from the highest levels of deprivation in the country, while other areas of Bradford are some of the least deprived in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Infant mortality is double the national average,<sup id="cite_ref-hsj.co.uk_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hsj.co.uk-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and life expectancy is slightly lower than in other parts of the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford" title="City of Bradford">district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The long-term health study <i>Born in Bradford</i> studied births in the city between 2007-2011 and found that the rate of birth defects was 3%, nearly twice the national average of 1.7%. The leading cause was found to be a 37% rate of <a href="/wiki/Consanguineous_marriage" class="mw-redirect" title="Consanguineous marriage">consanguineous marriage</a> among British South Asians, which had become more common than a generation earlier. A contributing cause was babies born to mothers over 34 years of age.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc4jul2013_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc4jul2013-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_Bradford" title="List of companies based in Bradford">List of companies based in Bradford</a></div>
<p>Bradford's textile industry has been in decline for many years and the city has suffered from de-industrialisation. Some areas of Bradford are among the worst levels of social deprivation in the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> with widespread pockets of exclusion, and rates of unemployment in some wards exceeding 25%,<sup id="cite_ref-fairuk.org_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fairuk.org-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> though other areas of Bradford are among the least deprived in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The economy is worth around £<a href="/wiki/List_of_UK_cities_by_GVA" title="List of UK cities by GVA">9.5</a>&#160;billion, making Bradford's economy a major powerhouse in the region and is forecast to grow to more than £10&#160;billion by 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> contributing around 8.4% of the region's output, and making the district the third largest (after Leeds and Sheffield) in Yorkshire &amp; Humber. The economy has diversified and the city is home to several major companies, notably in finance (<a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Building_Society" title="Yorkshire Building Society">Yorkshire Building Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Provident_Financial" title="Provident Financial">Provident Financial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santander_UK" title="Santander UK">Santander UK</a>), textiles ( <a href="/wiki/British_Wool_Marketing_Board" title="British Wool Marketing Board">British Wool Marketing Board</a>, Bulmer and Lumb Group), chemicals (<a href="/wiki/BASF" title="BASF">BASF</a>, Nufarm UK), electronics (<a href="/wiki/Arris_International" title="Arris International">Arris International</a>, Filtronic), engineering (NG Bailey, Powell Switchgear), and manufacturing, (Denso Marston, Bailey Offsite, <a href="/wiki/Hallmark_Cards" title="Hallmark Cards">Hallmark Cards</a> UK and <a href="/wiki/Seabrook_Potato_Crisps" title="Seabrook Potato Crisps">Seabrook Potato Crisps</a>). Supermarket chain <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a> has its head office in Bradford as does water utility company <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Water" title="Yorkshire Water">Yorkshire Water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the city's biggest employers is <a href="/wiki/Provident_Financial_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Provident Financial plc">Provident Financial plc</a>, a financial services group that specialises in <a href="/wiki/Moneylender" class="mw-redirect" title="Moneylender">Home Collected Credit (HCC)</a> and owns <a href="/wiki/Vanquis_Bank" title="Vanquis Bank">Vanquis Bank</a> which offers <a href="/wiki/Credit_cards" class="mw-redirect" title="Credit cards">credit cards</a>. It is listed on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100_Index" title="FTSE 100 Index">FTSE 100 Index</a>. The company was established in 1880 by Joshua Kelley Waddilove to provide affordable credit to families in <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> It has moved into a 250,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (23,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>), £45&#160;million, flagship <a href="/wiki/Headquarters" title="Headquarters">headquarters</a> building in the city centre creating hundreds of jobs for the city. The building also houses a 200-bed <a href="/wiki/Jurys_Inn" title="Jurys Inn">Jurys Inn</a> hotel.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2011 Plans to regenerate Bradford city centre, including the long-delayed Broadway shopping centre, was given a boost as Bradford Council secured £17.6&#160;million of regional growth funding from the government, which it will match to create a £35&#160;million "growth zone" in which companies would get business rate relief in exchange for helping people get training and jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2012 retail giant <a href="/wiki/Otto_GmbH" title="Otto GmbH">Freeman Grattan Holdings</a> secured a deal to open a new head office and house around 300 staff in the centre of Bradford. The mail order and online retailer will transfer office staff from its Lidget Green base, where Grattan has had a presence since 1934, to a Grade II-listed former wool warehouse on the edge of <a href="/wiki/Little_Germany,_Bradford" title="Little Germany, Bradford">Little Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Westfield_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Westfield Bradford">The Broadway</a> is the main retail shopping facility in Bradford. It includes <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marks_and_Spencer" class="mw-redirect" title="Marks and Spencer">Marks and Spencer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Next_plc" title="Next plc">Next</a>, <a href="/wiki/Superdry" title="Superdry">Superdry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schuh" title="Schuh">Schuh</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khaadi" title="Khaadi">Khaadi</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiko_(brand)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiko (brand) (page does not exist)">Kiko</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Menkind&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Menkind (page does not exist)">Menkind</a> among its over 70 units. It has car parking for 1,300 vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Kirkgate Shopping Centre is a shopping mall in Bradford city centre. It includes <a href="/wiki/Primark" title="Primark">Primark</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Look_(clothing_retailer)" class="mw-redirect" title="New Look (clothing retailer)">New Look</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/W_H_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="W H Smith">W H Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boots_UK" title="Boots UK">Boots</a>, <a href="/wiki/SportsDirect.com" class="mw-redirect" title="SportsDirect.com">SportsDirect.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Deichmann-Schuhe_GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinrich Deichmann-Schuhe GmbH">Deichmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/F._Hinds" title="F. Hinds">F. Hinds</a> in its 65 shops, as well as an indoor market and 550 car parking spaces. The centre has undergone a multimillion-pound refurbishment recently, and plans to upgrade the facade of the 1960s building have been submitted as it anticipates competition from the long-awaited £260&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Westfield_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Westfield Bradford">Westfield</a> development which opened on 5 November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thetelegraphandargus_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thetelegraphandargus-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Forster Square Shopping Park opened in 1995 and is adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Forster Square Railway Station</a>. It includes over 20 large retail and food units including <a href="/wiki/Next_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Next (clothing)">Next</a>, <a href="/wiki/TK_Maxx" title="TK Maxx">TK Maxx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harveys_Furniture" title="Harveys Furniture">Harveys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asda_Living" class="mw-redirect" title="Asda Living">Asda Living</a>, <a href="/wiki/Outfit_(retailer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Outfit (retailer)">Outfit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peacocks_(clothing)" title="Peacocks (clothing)">Peacocks</a>, <a href="/wiki/C._%26_J._Clark" title="C. &amp; J. Clark">Clarks</a>, <a href="/wiki/JD_Sports" title="JD Sports">JD Sports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Currys" title="Currys">Currys</a>, <a href="/wiki/DFS_(British_retailer)" class="mw-redirect" title="DFS (British retailer)">DFS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Costa_Coffee" title="Costa Coffee">Costa Coffee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sunbridge_Wells" title="Sunbridge Wells">Sunbridge Wells</a> is an underground retail complex, it incorporates restaurants, bars and retail units. The complex is built in a series of Victorian tunnels situated in the centre of Bradford.<sup id="cite_ref-otv_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otv-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Grade_I_listed_buildings_in_City_of_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Grade I listed buildings in City of Bradford">List of Grade I listed buildings in City of Bradford</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolling_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Bolling_Hall.jpg/220px-Bolling_Hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Bolling_Hall.jpg/330px-Bolling_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Bolling_Hall.jpg/440px-Bolling_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolling_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bolling_Hall,_Bradford" title="Bolling Hall, Bradford">Bolling Hall</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bradford's oldest building is the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">cathedral</a>, which for most of its life was a parish church. Few other <a href="/wiki/Medieval_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval era">Medieval</a> buildings have survived apart from <a href="/wiki/Bolling_Hall,_Bradford" title="Bolling Hall, Bradford">Bolling Hall</a>, which has been preserved as a museum.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Woolexchangebradford.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Woolexchangebradford.jpg/220px-Woolexchangebradford.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Woolexchangebradford.jpg/330px-Woolexchangebradford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Woolexchangebradford.jpg/440px-Woolexchangebradford.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Woolexchangebradford.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Wool_Exchange,_Bradford" title="Wool Exchange, Bradford">Wool Exchange, Bradford</a></div></div></div>
<p>There are some fine <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian buildings</a>: apart from the abundance of mills, there is the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Hall" title="Bradford City Hall">City Hall</a> (with statues of rulers of England unusually including <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>), the former <a href="/wiki/Wool_Exchange,_Bradford" title="Wool Exchange, Bradford">Wool Exchange</a>, and a large Victorian cemetery at Undercliffe. <a href="/wiki/Little_Germany,_Bradford" title="Little Germany, Bradford">Little Germany</a> is a splendid Victorian commercial district just east of the city centre which takes its name from 19th-century <a href="/wiki/German_Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="German Jewish">German Jewish</a> immigrants who ran businesses from some of the many <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a>. Following decades of decay there have been successful conversions to office and residential use. <a href="/wiki/Paper_Hall" title="Paper Hall">Paper Hall</a> was saved from demolition and renovated in the 1990s and in mid-2005 renovation began on the prominent Eastbrook Hall in Little Germany. This was opened as luxury apartments by <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Prince Charles</a> in Autumn 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_and_Argus_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_and_Argus-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Bradford also has a number of <a href="/wiki/Architecturally" class="mw-redirect" title="Architecturally">architecturally</a> historic hotels that date back to the establishment of the two railway lines into the city centre, back in <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> times. The Victoria Hotel and the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Hotel,_Bradford" title="Midland Hotel, Bradford">Midland Hotel</a> were built to accommodate business travellers to the city during the height of the woollen trade.
</p><p>Like many cities, Bradford lost a number of notable buildings to <a href="/wiki/Real_estate_developer" class="mw-redirect" title="Real estate developer">developers</a> in the 1960s and 1970s: particularly mourned at the time were the <a href="/wiki/Swan_Arcade,_Bradford" title="Swan Arcade, Bradford">Swan Arcade</a> and the old Kirkgate Market. In recent years some buildings from that era have themselves been demolished and replaced: Provincial House, next to Centenary Square, was demolished by controlled explosion in 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> and Forster House was pulled down in 2005 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Broadway,_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadway, Bradford">Broadway development</a>.
</p><p>Bradford's main art gallery is housed in the grand Edwardian <a href="/wiki/Cartwright_Hall" title="Cartwright Hall">Cartwright Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lister_Park" title="Lister Park">Lister Park</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a> celebrates cinema and movies, and is the most visited museum outside London. It contains an <a href="/wiki/Imax" class="mw-redirect" title="Imax">Imax</a> cinema, the <a href="/wiki/Cubby_Broccoli" class="mw-redirect" title="Cubby Broccoli">Cubby Broccoli</a> Cinema, and the <i>Pictureville</i> Cinema&#160;— described by David Puttnam as the best cinema in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Media_Museum_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Media_Museum-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg/220px-The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg/330px-The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg/440px-The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="4794" data-file-height="3175" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Alhambra_Theatre_Bradford.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Alhambra" title="Bradford Alhambra">Bradford Alhambra</a> frequently stages hit West End and Broadway musicals.</div></div></div>
<p>Also in the city is The <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Hall,_Bradford" title="St George&#39;s Hall, Bradford">St George's Hall</a>—a grand concert hall dating from 1853 making it the oldest concert hall in Britain and the third oldest in the whole of Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Alhambra" title="Bradford Alhambra">Alhambra</a> theatre, built in 1914 for theatre impresario Frank Laidler, and later owned by the Moss Empire group (<a href="/wiki/Oswald_Stoll" title="Oswald Stoll">Oswald Stoll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Moss" title="Edward Moss">Edward Moss</a>). The theatre was refurbished in 1986.
</p><p>Within the city district there are 37 parks and gardens. <a href="/wiki/Lister_Park" title="Lister Park">Lister Park</a>, with its boating lake and Mughal Water Gardens, was voted Britain's Best Park for 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Bowling Park in <a href="/wiki/East_Bowling" title="East Bowling">East Bowling</a> is the site of the annual Bradford Carnival celebrating local African and Caribbean culture.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Park" title="Bradford City Park">Bradford City Park</a>, now home to the Bradford Festival which includes the Mela, is a six-acre (2.4-hectare) public space in the heart of Bradford which contains the largest man-made water feature in any UK city—a 4,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (43,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) mirror pool featuring more than 100 fountains, including the tallest in any UK city at 30&#160;m (100&#160;ft). When the mirror pool is drained City Park is capable of holding events such as carnivals, markets, theatre productions, screenings and community festivals. Work started on the £24M project in February 2010 and City Park officially opened in March 2012, with thousands of people turning out for the grand opening event.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Park_Bradford.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/City_Park_Bradford.jpg/220px-City_Park_Bradford.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/City_Park_Bradford.jpg/330px-City_Park_Bradford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/City_Park_Bradford.jpg/440px-City_Park_Bradford.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3103" data-file-height="2073" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Park_Bradford.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Park" title="Bradford City Park">The Mirror Pool in City Park</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Odeon" title="Bradford Odeon">Bradford Odeon</a>, formerly the Gaumont and New Victoria Theatre, was built in 1930 as a music venue and cinema with a capacity of over 3,000, and was the largest UK cinema outside London at the time. (Another Odeon, always part of the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Cinemas" title="Odeon Cinemas">Odeon Cinemas</a> chain, was built in the city in 1938 and demolished in 1969.) Standing in a conservation area adjacent to the listed Alhambra Theatre, it closed in 2000 and was sold to developer Langtree with the intention it would be demolished and replaced with an apartment and office block. The Odeon was the subject of much controversy over these proposals, with public support in the form of a 10,000-signature petition and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cityoffilm.co.uk/">ongoing campaigns</a> for its renovation. In his successful by-election campaign for Bradford West in March 2012, <a href="/wiki/George_Galloway" title="George Galloway">George Galloway</a> cited the restoration of the Odeon as his number one priority, later asking Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> to intervene.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The architectural historian <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Foyle" title="Jonathan Foyle">Jonathan Foyle</a>, actresses <a href="/wiki/Imelda_Staunton" title="Imelda Staunton">Imelda Staunton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Agutter" title="Jenny Agutter">Jenny Agutter</a>, and director <a href="/wiki/Michael_Winner" title="Michael Winner">Michael Winner</a> all lent their support to the campaign.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorials">Memorials</span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Forster_Square_Station,_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Bradford_Forster_Square_Station%2C_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg/220px-Bradford_Forster_Square_Station%2C_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Bradford_Forster_Square_Station%2C_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg/330px-Bradford_Forster_Square_Station%2C_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Bradford_Forster_Square_Station%2C_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg/440px-Bradford_Forster_Square_Station%2C_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Forster_Square_Station,_Summer_2004_-_geograph.org.uk_-_84057.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Bradford Forster Square railway station</a></div></div></div>
<p>In past centuries Bradford's location in Bradfordale made communications difficult, except from the north. Nonetheless, Bradford is now well-served by transport systems. Bradford was first connected to the developing <a href="/wiki/Turnpike_trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Turnpike trust">turnpike</a> network in 1734,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> when the first <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a> turnpike was built between <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and Leeds via <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a> and Bradford.
</p><p>Today Bradford is accessed by several <a href="/wiki/Trunk_road" title="Trunk road">trunk roads</a>, the <a href="/wiki/A647_road" title="A647 road">A647</a> between Leeds and Halifax, via <a href="/wiki/Queensbury,_West_Yorkshire" title="Queensbury, West Yorkshire">Queensbury</a>, the <a href="/wiki/A650_road" title="A650 road">A650</a> between <a href="/wiki/Wakefield" title="Wakefield">Wakefield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keighley" title="Keighley">Keighley</a>, the <a href="/wiki/A658_road" title="A658 road">A658</a> to <a href="/wiki/Harrogate" title="Harrogate">Harrogate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/A6036_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A6036 road">A6036</a> to Halifax via <a href="/wiki/Shelf,_West_Yorkshire" title="Shelf, West Yorkshire">Shelf</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/M606_motorway" title="M606 motorway">M606</a>, a spur off the <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62</a> <a href="/wiki/Motorway" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway">motorway</a>, connects Bradford with the national motorway network. Although originally planned to go directly into the city centre it ends at the <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">ring road</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Canal" title="Bradford Canal">Bradford Canal</a> was a 4-mile (6.4&#160;km) spur from the <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> at <a href="/wiki/Shipley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Shipley, West Yorkshire">Shipley</a>. It was built to connect Bradford with the <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">quarries</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="North Riding of Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>, the industrial towns on both sides of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> and the ports of Liverpool and Goole. It opened in 1774, closed in 1866, reopened in 1871, and finally closed in 1922. There are plans to rebuild it as a key part of the regeneration of the city centre.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_station_entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bradford_station_entrance.jpg/220px-Bradford_station_entrance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bradford_station_entrance.jpg/330px-Bradford_station_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bradford_station_entrance.jpg/440px-Bradford_station_entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_station_entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford Interchange</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Bradford_Railway" title="Leeds and Bradford Railway">Leeds and Bradford Railway</a> opened <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Forster Square railway station</a> on 1 July 1846 with a service via Shipley to Leeds. The station was rebuilt in the early 1850s and again, in 1890 and 1990.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Lancashire_and_Yorkshire_Railway" title="Lancashire and Yorkshire Railway">Lancashire and Yorkshire Railway</a> opened a station at Drake Street on 9 May 1850, between <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Railway_(Great_Britain)" title="Great Northern Railway (Great Britain)">Great Northern Railway</a> opened a third terminus at <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Adolphus_Street_railway_station" title="Bradford Adolphus Street railway station">Adolphus Street</a> in 1854, but the station was too far from the centre, and the two companies built a joint station, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford Exchange</a> which opened in 1867.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Adolphus Street remained as a goods terminal. In 1973, Exchange station was rebuilt on a different site and in 1983 renamed <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford Interchange</a> and a bus station built alongside. Forster Square and Bradford Interchange stations are part of the West Yorkshire Metro.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road,_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road%2C_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg/220px-Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road%2C_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road%2C_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg/330px-Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road%2C_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road%2C_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg/440px-Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road%2C_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="539" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Trolleybus_in_Leeds_Road,_Greengates_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1463093.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Bradford" title="Trolleybuses in Bradford">Bradford trolleybus</a> in Leeds Road, Greengates, May 1971.</div></div></div>
<p>There have been many schemes to link between Bradford's railway terminals. The major redevelopment of the city centre in the 1960s provided an opportunity to connect the termini but was not pursued and large buildings were constructed on the alignment in the 1990s. The main difficulty in connecting the termini is the great difference in elevation: Bradford Interchange is at the end of a long slope, steep by railway standards, but is many feet higher than Forster Square. This gradient is not unprecedented in railway construction and the relocation of Forster Square further from the city centre has provided additional space in which the transition could be accomplished.
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tram</a> system was begun by Bradford Corporation in 1882. At first the vehicles were <a href="/wiki/Horsecar" title="Horsecar">horse-drawn</a> but were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine#steam_powered_vehicles" title="Steam engine">steam-driven</a> trams in 1883, and by <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric</a> vehicles in 1898. On 20 June 1911, Britain's first <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> systems opened simultaneously <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Bradford" title="Trolleybuses in Bradford">in Bradford</a>, between Laisterdyke and Dudley Hill, and <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Leeds" title="Trolleybuses in Leeds">in Leeds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-joyce-king-newman_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joyce-king-newman-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The last service in Bradford—and Britain—ceased operation on 26 March 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-joyce-king-newman_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joyce-king-newman-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Murray_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Ten Bradford trolleybuses are preserved at the <a href="/wiki/The_Trolleybus_Museum_at_Sandtoft" title="The Trolleybus Museum at Sandtoft">Sandtoft Trolleybus Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In 1974 Bradford's municipal buses were taken over by <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Metro" title="West Yorkshire Metro">West Yorkshire Metro</a>. <a href="/wiki/First_Bradford" title="First Bradford">First Bradford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Yorkshire" title="Arriva Yorkshire">Arriva Yorkshire</a> are the chief operators of buses in Bradford, with some routes using <a href="/wiki/Guided_bus" title="Guided bus">guided buses</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford Airport</a> is 6 miles (9.7&#160;km) to the north east of the city. Bradford and Leeds councils jointly opened the airport in 1931. There has been rapid expansion in recent years, and is the home base of economy Airline <a href="/wiki/Jet2.com" title="Jet2.com">Jet2.com</a>. In May 2007 the joint councils sold the airport to <a href="/wiki/Bridgepoint_Capital" title="Bridgepoint Capital">Bridgepoint Capital</a> for £145.5&#160;million. Bridgepoint announced that a further £70&#160;million would be invested in airport improvements, to boost passenger figures to over 7&#160;million by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Bradford" title="List of schools in Bradford">List of schools in Bradford</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_GS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Bradford_GS.jpg/200px-Bradford_GS.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Bradford_GS.jpg/300px-Bradford_GS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Bradford_GS.jpg/400px-Bradford_GS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_GS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_Grammar_School" title="Bradford Grammar School">Bradford Grammar School</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bradford_Grammar_School" title="Bradford Grammar School">Bradford Grammar School</a> was in existence near the parish church in the mid-16th century and re-established by Royal Charter as the Free <a href="/wiki/Grammar_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammar School">Grammar School</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> in 1662.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg/220px-University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg/330px-University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg/440px-University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Bradford_Richmond_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford" title="University of Bradford">University of Bradford</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford" title="University of Bradford">University of Bradford</a>, which has over 10,000 students, received its <a href="/wiki/Royal_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Charter">Royal Charter</a> in 1966, but traces its history to the 1860s when it was founded as the <i>Bradford Schools of Weaving, Design and Building</i>. The university now covers a wide range of subjects including technology and management science, optometry, pharmacy, medical sciences, nursing studies, archaeology and modern languages. Its <a href="/wiki/Peace_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace Studies">Peace Studies</a> department, founded with <a href="/wiki/Quaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker">Quaker</a> support in 1973, was for a long time the only such institution in the UK.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg/220px-University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg/330px-University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg/440px-University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4127" data-file-height="2454" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Bradford_school_of_management.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford_School_of_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Bradford School of Management">University of Bradford School of Management</a></div></div></div>
<p>In terms of nationally recognised leading areas of research there are various departments such as Institute of Cancer Therapeutics, Bradford School of Pharmacy, Peace Studies, Archaeology, Engineering, Management, Centre for Skin Sciences amongst others. The university balances academic research and teaching quality with a strong tradition of social inclusion. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford" title="University of Bradford">University of Bradford</a> was ranked second in the UK for graduate employment by the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> Supplement in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Bradford_Press_Release_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Bradford_Press_Release-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2010 the university was named as the greenest in the UK for the second year running.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_&amp;_Argus_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_&amp;_Argus-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_College.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bradford_College.JPG/220px-Bradford_College.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bradford_College.JPG/330px-Bradford_College.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bradford_College.JPG/440px-Bradford_College.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_College.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Old Building at <a href="/wiki/Bradford_College_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford College (England)">Bradford College</a> founded in 1832</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford_School_of_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Bradford School of Management">University of Bradford School of Management</a> located opposite Lister Park on Emm Lane, in 2011, was rated the 14th best business school in the UK by the <i>Financial Times</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Bradford_College_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford College (England)">Bradford College</a> developed from the 19th-century technical college whose buildings it inherited. It offers further and higher educational courses and is an Associate College of <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Metropolitan_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds Metropolitan University">Leeds Metropolitan University</a> and is the UK's largest provider of higher-education courses outside the university sector, with 23,000 students and 1,800 staff.<sup id="cite_ref-Yorkshire_forward_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yorkshire_forward-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> It absorbed the Art School whose most famous alumnus is <a href="/wiki/David_Hockney" title="David Hockney">David Hockney</a>.
</p><p>Whilst in Bradford after 1892, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_McMillan" title="Margaret McMillan">Margaret McMillan</a> joined the <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Society" title="Fabian Society">Fabian Society</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Labour_Party" title="Independent Labour Party">Independent Labour Party</a>. Working with her sister, Rachel, she set about improving the welfare of children living in the <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a>, and campaigned for free school meals. A memorial college to Margaret McMillan was opened in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recent <a href="/wiki/Ofsted" title="Ofsted">Ofsted</a> reports rank many Bradford schools as amongst the UK's finest.<sup id="cite_ref-Yorkshire_forward_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yorkshire_forward-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">Bradford Cathedral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Mahdi_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Mahdi Mosque">Al Mahdi Mosque</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg/200px-Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg/300px-Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg/400px-Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nave_of_Bradford_cathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">Bradford Cathedral</a></div></div></div>
<p>Two carved stones, probably parts of a <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Saxon</a> preaching cross, were found on the site of <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">Bradford Cathedral</a>. They indicate that Christians may have worshipped here since <a href="/wiki/Paulinus_of_York" title="Paulinus of York">Paulinus of York</a> came to the north of England in AD&#160;627 on a <a href="/wiki/Mission_(Christian)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mission (Christian)">mission</a> to convert <a href="/wiki/Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Northumbria">Northumbria</a>. He preached in <a href="/wiki/Dewsbury" title="Dewsbury">Dewsbury</a> and it was from there that Bradford was first evangelised. The vicars of Bradford later paid dues to that <a href="/wiki/Parish" title="Parish">parish</a>. The most prominent Christian church in Bradford is <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">Bradford Cathedral</a>, originally the <a href="/wiki/Parish_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Parish Church">Parish Church</a> of <a href="/wiki/St_Peter" class="mw-redirect" title="St Peter">St Peter</a>. The parish was in existence by 1283, and there was a stone church on the rock shelf above Bradford Beck by 1327. The <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Bradford" title="Diocese of Bradford">Diocese of Bradford</a> was created from part of the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Ripon" title="Diocese of Ripon">Diocese of Ripon</a> in 1919, and the church became a cathedral at that time. Many of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> churches that are found within the city are a legacy of the large <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> population that migrated to Bradford in the 19th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg/180px-Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg/270px-Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg/360px-Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hindu_Temple_-_Leeds_Road_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1003180.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_Lakshmi_Narayan_Hindu_Temple" title="Bradford Lakshmi Narayan Hindu Temple">Bradford Lakshmi Narayan Hindu Temple</a></div></div></div>
<p>The city has a sizeable Indian community and the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Lakshmi_Narayan_Hindu_Temple" title="Bradford Lakshmi Narayan Hindu Temple">Lakshmi Narayan mandir</a> which opened in April 2008<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> temple in northern England.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> There is a Hindu temple and community centre on Thornton Lane<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> and smaller house-based mandirs, as shown in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Hindu_temples_in_England#North_East" title="List of Hindu temples in England">List of Hindu Temples in England</a>.
</p><p>The patron saint of Bradford is <a href="/wiki/Saint_Blaise" title="Saint Blaise">Saint Blaise</a> because of his patronage of wool combing, and his statue features on the Wool Exchange in the centre of the city. There is also a statue of the saint in St Cuthbert's Catholic Church, Wilmer Road, also noted as the location of the famous Stations of the Cross by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gill" title="Eric Gill">Eric Gill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sikh" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikh">Sikh</a> community has six <a href="/wiki/Gurudwara" class="mw-redirect" title="Gurudwara">gurudwaras</a> in the city. The Sikh festival of <a href="/wiki/Vaisakhi" title="Vaisakhi">Vaisakhi</a> is celebrated on 14 April. Sikhs travel to each of the gurudwaras in the city in a procession called a <i>nagar kirtan</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c9/Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg/220px-Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c9/Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg/330px-Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c9/Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg/440px-Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="655" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_Bradford_Reform_Synagogue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Tree_of_Life_Synagogue" title="Bradford Tree of Life Synagogue">Bradford Tree of Life Synagogue</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> community was strong in the middle to late 19th century and built <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Reform_Synagogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford Reform Synagogue">Bradford Reform Synagogue</a> in Manningham. This, "The oldest <a href="/wiki/Reform_synagogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Reform synagogue">reform synagogue</a> outside London",<sup id="cite_ref-open_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> was established by <a href="/wiki/German_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="German Jews">German Jews</a> who had moved to Bradford for the wool trade. According to historian Sharman Kadish, "The city of Bradford was unique in that it boasted a reform synagogue before it acquired an orthodox one".<sup id="cite_ref-Kadish_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kadish-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In 1881 <a href="/wiki/Russian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Jews">Russian Jews</a> made their home in Bradford, having fled their homeland, and founded an orthodox synagogue.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
In 2011 the Jewish population was 299.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
