<p>The district has a tradition of <a href="/wiki/Nonconformism" class="mw-redirect" title="Nonconformism">nonconformity</a> which is reflected in the number of chapels erected by <a href="/wiki/Congregationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregationalist">Congregationalists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodists</a>. The city was a centre of the <a href="/wiki/House_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="House Church">House Church</a> movement in the 1980s, and the Christian charity <a href="/wiki/Christians_Against_Poverty" title="Christians Against Poverty">Christians Against Poverty</a> was founded in the city. Other house churches in the city include <a href="/wiki/El_Shaddai_International_Christian_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="El Shaddai International Christian Centre">El Shaddai International Christian Centre</a> and the World Outreach Church. Bradford is also home to the  <a href="/wiki/LIFE_Church_UK" title="LIFE Church UK">LIFE Church UK</a>, a large nonconforming Church, that has around 3,000 members.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a> hosts the Bradford International Film Festival annually in March.
In June 2009 Bradford was designated the world's first <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> City of Film for its links to the <a href="/wiki/Film_production" class="mw-redirect" title="Film production">production</a> and distribution of films, its media and film museum and its "cinematographic legacy".
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg/220px-Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg/330px-Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg/440px-Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a>, Bradford</div></div></div>
<p>"Becoming the world's first City of Film is the ultimate celebration of Bradford's established and dynamic history in film and media," said Colin Philpott, director of Bradford's National Media Museum. "With the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Film" title="City of Film">UNESCO City of Film</a> designation, Bradford will now go on to achieve inspirational projects in film." <a href="/wiki/Simon_Beaufoy" title="Simon Beaufoy">Simon Beaufoy</a> from Bradford, the Oscar-winning screenwriter of <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i>, said the city had played a crucial role in the story of <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking" title="Filmmaking">cinema</a> and deserved to be recognised.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradford_named_City_of_Film_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradford_named_City_of_Film-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Bradford has developed a relationship with <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>, hosting the <a href="/wiki/International_Film_Festival_of_India" title="International Film Festival of India">International Indian Film Festival</a> awards in 2007.
</p><p>The Bradford Animation Festival is the UK's longest-running <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animation</a> festival. Held each November, the festival hosts an array of screentalks, workshops and special events. The festival culminates in the annual BAF Awards which celebrate new animation from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cottingley,_Bradford" title="Cottingley, Bradford">Cottingley</a> Fairy photographs taken by <a href="/wiki/Elsie_Wright" class="mw-redirect" title="Elsie Wright">Elsie Wright</a> and two of the cameras used are on display in the Kodak Gallery in the National Science and Media Museum in Bradford.
</p><p>There are four theatres in Bradford. The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Alhambra" title="Bradford Alhambra">Alhambra</a> also has a smaller studio theatre in the same complex. These are operated by <a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford" title="City of Bradford">City of Bradford</a> Metropolitan District Council. The Theatre in the Mill is a small studio theatre at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford" title="University of Bradford">University of Bradford</a>, which presents student and community shows and small-scale touring professional work. The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Playhouse" title="Bradford Playhouse">Bradford Playhouse</a> is a privately run venue with a medium-sized proscenium theatre and a small studio.
</p><p>Among the professional theatre companies based in Bradford are <i>Kala Sangam</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Satirical" class="mw-redirect" title="Satirical">satirical</a> madcap comedy troop, <i>Komedy Kollective</i>, <i>Lost Dog</i> (based at Theatre In The Mill) and <i>Mind the Gap</i>, one of the longest established, who have always worked with a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disabled</a> and able-bodied performers. Groups and organisations teaching theatre include The <i>Asian Theatre School</i>, Bradford Stage and Theatre School and <i>Stage 84</i>. There are also a number of amateur theatre groups.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Hall,_Bradford" title="St George&#39;s Hall, Bradford">St George's Hall</a> is a concert hall dating from 1853 making it the oldest concert hall in Britain and the third oldest in Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Festival_Choral_Society" title="Bradford Festival Choral Society">Bradford Festival Choral Society</a> was founded to perform at the inaugural <i>Bradford Musical Festival</i> that took place in August of that year,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> and the choir is still a part of the musical life of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Hall%C3%A9_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Hallé Orchestra">Hallé Orchestra</a> have been regular visitors over the years, as have a wide range of popular musicians, bands, entertainers, comedians and theatrical productions.
In 2017 an £8.2 million renovation scheme of St George's Hall was started, after completion it is planned for the concert venue to re-open in late 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg/220px-St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg/330px-St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg/440px-St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Georges_Hall_Bradford.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St George's Hall</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cinemas" class="mw-redirect" title="Cinemas">Cinemas</a> have been replaced by vast entertainment complexes with multi-screen cinemas. The <i>Leisure Exchange</i> in the city centre has a 16 screen Cineworld. At <a href="/wiki/Thornbury,_West_Yorkshire" title="Thornbury, West Yorkshire">Thornbury</a>, on the outskirts is the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Leeds-Bradford" title="Odeon Leeds-Bradford">Odeon Leeds-Bradford</a> with 13 screens which replaced the old Odeon next to the Alhambra which is the continuing focus of protests by Bradfordians who do not wish to see the old building demolished.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The University of Bradford also has a cinema run by the Students' Union, operating from the University's Great Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nightlife in Bradford has traditionally centred on Manor Row and Manningham Lane. More recently, several clubs and <a href="/wiki/Pub" title="Pub">pubs</a> have opened in the West End of Bradford, around the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Alhambra" title="Bradford Alhambra">Alhambra Theatre</a>, turning what was a previously fairly quiet area into one that is often crowded and vibrant at night. North Parade has also seen several new themed bars open and is at the heart of the Independent Quarter of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sunbridge_Wells" title="Sunbridge Wells">Sunbridge Wells</a> is an underground leisure and retail complex which opened in Bradford city centre in 2016.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG/220px-Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG/330px-Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG/440px-Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sunny_day_in_the_Bradford_City_Park.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sunny day at the City Park</div></div></div>
<p>Bradford was one of the first areas of the UK to get a local commercial radio station <a href="/wiki/Pennine_Radio_(radio_station)" title="Pennine Radio (radio station)">Pennine Radio</a> in September 1975. Today this is <a href="/wiki/The_Pulse_of_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="The Pulse of West Yorkshire">The Pulse of West Yorkshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulse_Classic_Gold" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulse Classic Gold">Pulse Classic Gold</a>. As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bradford&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Bradford Community Broadcasting based in the city centre has broadcast on full-time Community Radio licence around Bradford and the Aire Valley, whilst the University radio station <a href="/wiki/Ramair" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramair">Ramair</a> broadcasts to the student population. Bradford's only television station <a href="/wiki/AAP_TV" title="AAP TV">AAP TV</a> caters for Bradford's large Asian community. The <i><a href="/wiki/Telegraph_and_Argus" class="mw-redirect" title="Telegraph and Argus">Telegraph and Argus</a></i> is Bradford's daily newspaper, published six days each week from Monday to Saturday.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Mela" title="Bradford Mela">Bradford Mela</a> is now part of the bigger <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bradford Festival (page does not exist)">Bradford Festival</a> which takes place in June.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> The word <a href="/wiki/Mela" title="Mela">mela</a> is <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> for 'a gathering' or 'to meet'. In the UK, melas provide an opportunity for communities to come together to celebrate and share their cultures. Mela festivals include a combination of <a href="/wiki/Market_(place)" class="mw-redirect" title="Market (place)">markets</a>, funfairs, food and drink, arts and workshops, children's activities, strolling entertainment and a variety of music and dance performances on a number of stages. Bradford held the first mela in Europe in September 1988 and it is presently held in Bradford City Park.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Park" title="Bradford City Park">Bradford City Park</a> has the largest city centre water feature in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_art_galleries">Museums and art galleries</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cartwright_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Cartwright_Hall.jpg/220px-Cartwright_Hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Cartwright_Hall.jpg/330px-Cartwright_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Cartwright_Hall.jpg/440px-Cartwright_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2167" data-file-height="1850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cartwright_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cartwright_Hall" title="Cartwright Hall">Cartwright Hall</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bradford is home to the acclaimed <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a> (previously the National Museum of Photography, Film &amp; Television) which celebrates cinema and movies, and is the most visited museum outside London. It contains the UK's first <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theatre, the <a href="/wiki/Cubby_Broccoli" class="mw-redirect" title="Cubby Broccoli">Cubby Broccoli</a> Cinema, and the <a href="/wiki/Pictureville_Cinema" title="Pictureville Cinema">Pictureville Cinema</a>&#160;— described by <a href="/wiki/David_Puttnam" title="David Puttnam">David Puttnam</a> as the best cinema in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Media_Museum_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Media_Museum-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bradford_Industrial_Museum" title="Bradford Industrial Museum">Bradford Industrial Museum</a> was established in 1974 at Moorside Mills, a spinning mill in <a href="/wiki/Eccleshill,_West_Yorkshire" title="Eccleshill, West Yorkshire">Eccleshill</a>. The Museum celebrates and explains the significant achievements in Bradford's industrial past, from textiles and printing to the manufacture of motor cars.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A mile from the city centre is <a href="/wiki/Bolling_Hall,_Bradford" title="Bolling Hall, Bradford">Bolling Hall</a> Museum, a part <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> building which offers visitors a journey through the lives and times of the families for which it provided a home for over five hundred years. Rooms are furnished and decorated to give a taste of life at different periods of the house's history.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford's main art gallery is housed in <a href="/wiki/Cartwright_Hall" title="Cartwright Hall">Cartwright Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lister_Park" title="Lister Park">Lister Park</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bradford_1_Gallery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bradford 1 Gallery (page does not exist)">Bradford 1 Gallery</a> is a city centre <a href="/wiki/Art_gallery" class="mw-redirect" title="Art gallery">art gallery</a> opened in October 2007 in a new building in Centenary Square. The gallery shows four temporary <a href="/wiki/Exhibitions" class="mw-redirect" title="Exhibitions">exhibitions</a> a year.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Impressions_Gallery" title="Impressions Gallery">Impressions Gallery</a> is an independent contemporary photography gallery with a temporary exhibitions programme showing on average six exhibitions each year. The gallery moved from York to Centenary Square, Bradford, in 2007.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<p>Bradford is the home town of rock bands, <a href="/wiki/New_Model_Army_(band)" title="New Model Army (band)">New Model Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti_System" title="Anti System">Anti System</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smokie_(band)" title="Smokie (band)">Smokie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Death_Cult" title="Southern Death Cult">Southern Death Cult</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Cult" title="The Cult">The Cult</a>, The Scene, Redwire, <a href="/wiki/Chantel_McGregor" title="Chantel McGregor">The Chantel McGregor Band</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_Minute_Silence" title="One Minute Silence">One Minute Silence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scars_on_45" title="Scars on 45">Scars on 45</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrorvision" title="Terrorvision">Terrorvision</a>, <a href="/wiki/My_Dying_Bride" title="My Dying Bride">My Dying Bride</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> group <a href="/wiki/Fun-Da-Mental" title="Fun-Da-Mental">Fun-Da-Mental</a>.
</p><p>Singer-Songwriters <a href="/wiki/Tasmin_Archer" title="Tasmin Archer">Tasmin Archer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Kills" class="mw-redirect" title="Natalia Kills">Natalia Kills</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kiki_Dee" title="Kiki Dee">Kiki Dee</a>—the first white British artist to be signed by <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown</a>, also hail from the City.
</p><p>In 2002 <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Gates" title="Gareth Gates">Gareth Gates</a> came second in the first series of <a href="/wiki/Pop_Idol" title="Pop Idol">Pop Idol</a> and went on to achieve 4 UK number one singles before enjoying success in <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">Musical theatre</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Walsh" class="mw-redirect" title="Kimberly Walsh">Kimberly Walsh</a> achieved major success after winning a place in the girl band <a href="/wiki/Girls_Aloud" title="Girls Aloud">Girls Aloud</a> in <a href="/wiki/Popstars:_The_Rivals" title="Popstars: The Rivals">Popstars: The Rivals</a> later in the same year, and in 2010 <a href="/wiki/Zayn_Malik" title="Zayn Malik">Zayn Malik</a> came third in <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i> with his boy band <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a>, who in March 2012 became the first British group to go straight to the top of the US music charts with their debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The guitar player and composer <a href="/wiki/Allan_Holdsworth" title="Allan Holdsworth">Allan Holdsworth</a> was born in Bradford in 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Curry_Capital_of_Britain">Curry Capital of Britain</span></h3>
<p>In 2013 Bradford was again crowned "Curry Capital of Britain" after seeing off other strong contenders such as <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton" title="Wolverhampton">Wolverhampton</a>. Bradford scored highly not just for the quality of food and service offered by each of the restaurants, but also for food hygiene, a deep understanding of the curry restaurant sector and its success in collectively raising funds for food charity The Curry Tree, which seeks to alleviate the plight of the poor in South East Asia. The judges were also particularly impressed by Bradford's International Food Academy and <a href="/wiki/Jamie%27s_Ministry_of_Food" title="Jamie&#39;s Ministry of Food">Jamie's Ministry of Food</a>, which teaches the districts residents how to cook quick, simple, healthy and cost-effective meals.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h2>
<p>Bradford has a long sporting tradition, and <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Bulls</a>, formerly Bradford Northern, is one of the most successful <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> clubs in the world, winning the World Club Championship three times since 2002 and seven times winners of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Football League Championship">Rugby Football League Championship</a>. Bradford Bulls play at the <a href="/wiki/Grattan_Stadium,_Odsal" class="mw-redirect" title="Grattan Stadium, Odsal">Grattan Stadium, Odsal</a>, formerly Odsal Stadium. The city is also home to a number of rugby union clubs—Bradford Salem are based in the Heaton area and Wibsey RFC can be found to the south of the city centre. The <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dunn_(boxer)" title="Richard Dunn (boxer)">Richard Dunn</a> Sports Centre is located close to the Odsal and the sports facilities at the university are also open to the public at certain times.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade,_Bradford.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Valley_Parade%2C_Bradford.jpg/220px-Valley_Parade%2C_Bradford.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Valley_Parade%2C_Bradford.jpg/330px-Valley_Parade%2C_Bradford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Valley_Parade%2C_Bradford.jpg/440px-Valley_Parade%2C_Bradford.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valley_Parade,_Bradford.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_A.F.C." title="Bradford City A.F.C.">Bradford City's</a> <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> stadium</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_A.F.C." title="Bradford City A.F.C.">Bradford City Football Club</a> was formed in 1903. James Whyte, a sub-editor of the <i>Bradford Observer</i> met with <a href="/wiki/Football_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Association">Football Association</a> representative, John Brunt, in January to discuss plans, and in May, <a href="/wiki/Manningham_F.C." title="Manningham F.C.">Manningham RFC</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> team decided to change codes to <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-frost_p11_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frost_p11-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> subsequently elected Bradford City to the league, with a total of 30 votes to replace <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Rovers_F.C." title="Doncaster Rovers F.C.">Doncaster Rovers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> because it saw the invitation as a chance to introduce football to the rugby-dominated county.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Eight years after the club was elected to the league, City won the <a href="/wiki/1911_FA_Cup_Final" title="1911 FA Cup Final">FA Cup</a> and recorded the highest league position in its history.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> They currently compete in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">Football League One</a>, the third tier of English football. The ground suffered one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_accidents_and_disasters_by_death_toll#Sporting_events" title="List of accidents and disasters by death toll">worst all-time sporting disasters</a> after <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_stadium_fire" title="Bradford City stadium fire">56&#160;people died</a> at <a href="/wiki/Valley_Parade" title="Valley Parade">Valley Parade</a> on 11 May 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> A second club from the city, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Park_Avenue_A.F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford Park Avenue A.F.C.">Bradford Park Avenue</a> played in <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">the Football League</a> until it dropped out in 1970, then went into liquidation in 1974. The club now plays in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_North" title="National League North">National League North</a>, which means the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_derby" title="Bradford derby">Bradford derby</a> has not been played in years. Bradford Park Avenue hosted county cricket for <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire</a> as well as football.
</p><p>The defunct <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Dukes" title="Bradford Dukes">Bradford Dukes</a> <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">speedway</a> team raced at Odsal. Speedway was staged at Greenfields Stadium in the pioneer days, when it was known as the Autodrome in the early 1960s. Odsal opened its doors in 1945 and continued in the late 1950s. It entered a team in the 1960 Provincial League then fell dormant until the 1970s when it re-opened. The track staged a Speedway World Final. The speedway team rode under a number of names—probably the longest running was Bradford Northern—in common with the Rugby League team. This was changed to Bradford Barons—emulating the more successful Halifax Dukes. Eventually the Halifax team was brought to Bradford under the name Bradford Dukes.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Joe_Johnson_(snooker_player)" title="Joe Johnson (snooker player)">Joe Johnson</a> is a retired professional snooker player from Bradford who won the <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Snooker_Championship" title="1986 World Snooker Championship">1986 World Snooker Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Dragons" title="Bradford Dragons">Bradford Dragons</a> are the city's basketball team, competing in the second tier <a href="/wiki/English_Basketball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="English Basketball League">English Basketball League</a> Division 1. The team are coached by Chris Mellor and play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Bradford_College" title="Bradford College">Bradford College</a>. The team are having a strong season, and are on courseto reach the post season playoffs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="City_of_Sanctuary">City of Sanctuary</span></h2>
<p>After a campaign in 2008, Bradford was recognised as a 'City of Sanctuary' on 18 November 2010. Bradford is "a place where a broad range of local organisations, <a href="/wiki/Community" title="Community">community</a> groups and <a href="/wiki/Faith" title="Faith">faith</a> communities, as well as <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">local government</a> are publicly committed to welcoming and including people seeking sanctuary." The city has a history of welcoming and including newcomers from throughout the world. An example of this was Bradford's purchase of the Carlton Hostel building in 1939 as part of a <i><a href="/wiki/Kindertransport" title="Kindertransport">Kindertransport</a></i> scheme, made possible through donations from both Bradford's Jewish community and non–Jews,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> to house <a href="/wiki/German_Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="German Jewish">German Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugee</a> <a href="/wiki/Children" class="mw-redirect" title="Children">children</a> during the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg/220px-Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg/330px-Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg/440px-Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_Royal_Infirmary_-_geograph.org.uk_-_34416.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_Royal_Infirmary" title="Bradford Royal Infirmary">Bradford Royal Infirmary</a></div></div></div>
<p>There are two major hospitals in Bradford: <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Royal_Infirmary" title="Bradford Royal Infirmary">Bradford Royal Infirmary</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Luke%27s_Hospital,_Bradford" title="St. Luke&#39;s Hospital, Bradford">St Luke's Hospital</a>. Both are teaching hospitals and are operated by Bradford Teaching Hospitals NHS trust. Over the years the Trust has subsumed a number of smaller hospitals; these include Woodlands Orthopaedic Hospital, Northern View and Bierley Hall.
</p><p>Bradford is the focus of one of the UK's largest ever birth cohort studies, known as <i><a href="/wiki/Born_in_Bradford" title="Born in Bradford">Born in Bradford</a></i>. Partly supported by European funding, it is the result of close collaboration between the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford" title="University of Bradford">University of Bradford</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">NHS</a> and other institutions in West Yorkshire. It will track the lives of all the babies born in the city from 2006 to 2008 and aims to provide a wealth of data, allowing health researchers the opportunity to investigate many different aspects of health and wellbeing.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span></h2>
<p>Bradford has been the scene of some high-profile crimes such as the shooting of Bradford PC <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Beshenivsky" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharon Beshenivsky">Sharon Beshenivsky</a> while responding to a burglary in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In May 2010, Stephen Griffiths was charged with the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_murders" title="Bradford murders">Bradford murders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Manningham_Riot" class="mw-redirect" title="Manningham Riot">Manningham Riot</a> occurred between 10 and 12 June 1995, in <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2001_Bradford_race_riots" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 Bradford race riots">2001 Bradford race riots</a> began on 7 July 2001 as a result of tension between <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minority" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic minority">ethnic minority</a> communities and the city's white majority, stoked by the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Nazi_League" title="Anti-Nazi League">Anti-Nazi League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_National_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="British National Front">National Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> There were 297 arrests; 187 people charged with riot, 45 with violent disorder leading to 200 jail sentences totalling 604 years.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bradfordians">Bradfordians</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Bradford" title="List of people from Bradford">List of people from Bradford</a></div>
<p><i>Only a few particularly notable names are listed here.</i>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:170px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_William_Rothenstein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/33/Sir_William_Rothenstein.jpg" decoding="async" width="168" height="194" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="168" data-file-height="194" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_William_Rothenstein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Rothenstein" title="William Rothenstein">Sir William Rothenstein</a>  photo by George Charles Beresford, 1902</div></div></div>
<p>Among Bradford born people who made significant contributions to the arts were <a href="/wiki/David_Hockney" title="David Hockney">David Hockney</a>, painter, draughtsman, printmaker, stage designer and photographer, who was born in the city and educated at <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Grammar_School" title="Bradford Grammar School">Bradford Grammar School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Delius" title="Frederick Delius">Frederick Delius</a> (1862–1934) was a composer born to a family of German descent in the city<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/J.B._Priestley" class="mw-redirect" title="J.B. Priestley">J.B. Priestley</a> (1894–1984) was a novelist and playwright. <a href="/wiki/William_Rothenstein" title="William Rothenstein">Sir William Rothenstein</a> was a painter, draughtsman and writer on art who was principal of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Art" title="Royal College of Art">Royal College of Art</a> from 1920 to 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In the genre of classical music  <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Friend" title="Rodney Friend">Rodney Friend</a> is an English violinist, born (1940), In 1964 he became the youngest ever leader of the <a href="/wiki/London_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="London Philharmonic Orchestra">London Philharmonic Orchestra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In the field of science and medicine, <a href="/wiki/Friederich_Wilhelm_Eurich" title="Friederich Wilhelm Eurich">Friederich Wilhelm Eurich</a> (1867–1945), professor of forensic medicine and bacteriologist, did much to conquer <a href="/wiki/Anthrax" title="Anthrax">anthrax</a> in the wool trade.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Appleton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Appleton.jpg/150px-Appleton.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Appleton.jpg/225px-Appleton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/58/Appleton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Appleton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sir_Edward_Appleton" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Edward Appleton">Sir Edward Appleton</a></div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Edward_Victor_Appleton" title="Edward Victor Appleton">Sir Edward Appleton</a> (1892–1965), discoverer of the <a href="/wiki/Ionosphere" title="Ionosphere">ionosphere</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winner.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lowry_Turner" title="Robert Lowry Turner">Professor Robert Turner</a> (1923–1990) was a pathologist who came to Bradford from Belfast, and pioneered the use of <a href="/wiki/Chemotherapy" title="Chemotherapy">chemotherapy</a> in the treatment of cancer at the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Royal_Infirmary" title="Bradford Royal Infirmary">Bradford Royal Infirmary</a>.
</p><p>In the field of industry, Sir <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Behrens" title="Jacob Behrens">Jacob Behrens</a> (1806–1889) was an Anglo–German textile merchant who was instrumental in Bradford becoming a major exporter of woollen goods.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A social reformer who campaigned against child labour, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Oastler" title="Richard Oastler">Richard Oastler</a> (1789–1861), is commemorated by a statue in Northgate<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and the Oastler Shopping Centre located close to the Kirkgate Shopping Centre  <a href="/wiki/William_Edward_Forster" title="William Edward Forster">W.E. Forster</a> (1818–1886), was MP for Bradford and, commemorated by statue, is the namesake of Forster Square.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In recent pop culture the former participant of <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Zayn_Malik" title="Zayn Malik">Zayn Malik</a>, former member of successful<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boy_band" title="Boy band">boy band</a> <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a>, was born and raised in Bradford.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> American film star <a href="/wiki/Aasif_Mandvi" title="Aasif Mandvi">Aasif Mandvi</a> grew up in Bradford.<sup id="cite_ref-Garner_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garner-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bradford&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Bradford%22">"Bradford"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Bradford%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Bradford%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Bradford%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Bradford%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Bradford%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The city has a rich heritage in <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">film</a> production and many films and <a href="/wiki/TV" class="mw-redirect" title="TV">TV</a> productions have been filmed in the city. Films using Bradford as a location include <i><a href="/wiki/Room_at_the_Top_(1959_film)" title="Room at the Top (1959 film)">Room at the Top</a></i> (1959), <i><a href="/wiki/Billy_Liar_(film)" title="Billy Liar (film)">Billy Liar</a></i> (1963) and the  television adaptation of the <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Riding" title="Red Riding">Red Riding</a></i> works by <a href="/wiki/David_Peace" title="David Peace">David Peace</a> first broadcast in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford was the location for the films <i><a href="/wiki/Yanks" title="Yanks">Yanks</a></i> (1979), starring <a href="/wiki/Richard_Gere" title="Richard Gere">Richard Gere</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Railway_Children_(1970_film)" title="The Railway Children (1970 film)">The Railway Children</a></i> (1970) starring <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Agutter" title="Jenny Agutter">Jenny Agutter</a>, a children's film shot around <a href="/wiki/Haworth" title="Haworth">Haworth</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Bronte_Parsonage" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronte Parsonage">Bronte Parsonage</a> about <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> children whose father goes missing and <i><a href="/wiki/FairyTale:_A_True_Story" title="FairyTale: A True Story">FairyTale: A True Story</a></i> (1997) starring <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Keitel" title="Harvey Keitel">Harvey Keitel</a> based on the story of the <a href="/wiki/Cottingley_Fairies" title="Cottingley Fairies">Cottingley Fairies</a>.
</p><p>In the BBC political satire <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Mrs_Pritchard" title="The Amazing Mrs Pritchard">The Amazing Mrs Pritchard</a></i> (2006), the Prime Minister considers a proposal to move Parliament to Bradford, as it is closer to the geographic centre of the country than London. The <a href="/wiki/Buttershaw" title="Buttershaw">Buttershaw</a> area of the city featured in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Rita,_Sue_and_Bob_Too" title="Rita, Sue and Bob Too">Rita, Sue and Bob Too</a></i> (1987), in which two 16-year-old girls were involved in a love triangle with a wealthy married man (played by <a href="/wiki/George_Costigan" title="George Costigan">George Costigan</a>). The film was created by local <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Dunbar" title="Andrea Dunbar">Andrea Dunbar</a>, and was initially unpopular with local residents due to its negative image of the area, but has since earned itself a good reputation in the local community as Buttershaw's claim to fame.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford features in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_The_Meaning_of_Life" title="Monty Python&#39;s The Meaning of Life">Monty Python's The Meaning of Life</a></i> (1983) with footage filmed in <a href="/wiki/Lister_Park" title="Lister Park">Lister Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/Spooks_(TV_series)" title="Spooks (TV series)">Spooks</a></i> spin-off for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">BBC Three</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Spooks:_Code_9" title="Spooks: Code 9">Spooks: Code 9</a></i>, was filmed in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford is also in the film <i><a href="/wiki/East_Is_East_(1999_film)" title="East Is East (1999 film)">East is East</a></i>. Oak Lane is shown in the film when the family visit the city.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford was the focus of a 2012 <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> documentary, <i><a href="/wiki/Make_Bradford_British" title="Make Bradford British">Make Bradford British</a></i>, which examined the level of integration between the city's Christian and Muslim communities.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Series 2 of <a href="/wiki/The_Syndicate_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Syndicate (TV series)"><i>The Syndicate</i></a>, which aired in 2013 on BBC One, featured a syndicate involving workers at a public hospital in Bradford.
</p><p>In the 1993 novel <a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_(Swindells_novel)" title="Stone Cold (Swindells novel)"><i>Stone Cold</i></a>, the main character Link is from Bradford.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mott_The_Hoople" class="mw-redirect" title="Mott The Hoople">Mott The Hoople</a> mention Bradford in their song “All the way from Memphis”: “Now it's a mighty long way down rock'n'roll, through the Bradford Cities and the Oreoles.”
</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Mekons" title="The Mekons">The Mekons</a> (who formed in nearby <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>) mention Bradford in the song "Ghosts of American Astronauts": “Up in the hills above Bradford / Outside the napalm factory”.
</p><p>The award-winning 2013 film <a href="/wiki/The_Selfish_Giant_(2013_film)" title="The Selfish Giant (2013 film)"><i>The Selfish Giant</i></a> takes place in and around Bradford.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford features under the name of "Broadbeck" in the best-selling 1912 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Windyridge" title="Windyridge">Windyridge</a></i> by Bradford novelist <a href="/wiki/Willie_Riley" title="Willie Riley">Willie Riley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-copeland_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-copeland-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span></h2>
<p>Bradford is twinned with a number of places around the world:<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia"><img alt="North Macedonia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg/23px-Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg/35px-Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg/46px-Flag_of_North_Macedonia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1680" data-file-height="840" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Skopje" title="Skopje">Skopje</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> (since 1963)<sup id="cite_ref-Skopje_twinnings_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skopje_twinnings-184">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Roubaix" title="Roubaix">Roubaix</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (since 1969)<sup id="cite_ref-Archant_twinning_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archant_twinning-185">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium"><img alt="Belgium" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Verviers" title="Verviers">Verviers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> (since 1970)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Mönchengladbach">Mönchengladbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (since 1971)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland"><img alt="Republic of Ireland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Flag_of_Ireland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Ireland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> (since 1987)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan"><img alt="Pakistan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Mirpur,_Azad_Kashmir" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirpur, Azad Kashmir">Mirpur, Azad Kashmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> (friendship agreement in 1998)</li></ul>

Heritage Cartography. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-903004-34-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-903004-34-0"><bdi>978-1-903004-34-0</bdi></a>. <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/63800551">63800551</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Ordnance+Survey+1%3A10%2C560+County+Series+Map%3A+Yorkshire+Sheet+216&amp;rft.pub=Heritage+Cartography&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F63800551&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-903004-34-0&amp;rft.aulast=Adams&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter+J.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABradford" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> This was surveyed 1847–1850, and published in 1852, though it was reprinted at various dates with certain (unidentified) details updated. Ryburn. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-85331-004-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-85331-004-1"><bdi>978-1-85331-004-1</bdi></a>. <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/63989031">63989031</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Ryburn+Map+of+Victorian+Bradford&amp;rft.pub=Ryburn&amp;rft.date=1987&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F63989031&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-85331-004-1&amp;rft.aulast=Wilmott&amp;rft.aufirst=Elvira&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABradford" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> The map itself is a reproduction of the <i>Plan of the Town of Bradford … revised and corrected to the present time by Dixon &amp; Hindle</i>, 1871.</li>
<li><cite class="citation book">Richardson, C. (1976). <i>A Geography of Bradford</i>. University of Bradford. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0_901945_19_6" title="Special:BookSources/0 901945 19 6"><bdi>0 901945 19 6</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+Geography+of+Bradford&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Bradford&amp;rft.date=1976&amp;rft.isbn=0901945196&amp;rft.aulast=Richardson&amp;rft.aufirst=C.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABradford" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></li></ul>
